 Anas bin Malik narrated that :
the Messenger of Allah said:   Whoever prays Fajr in congregation, then sits remembering Allah until the sun has risen, then he prays two Rak'ah, then for him is the reward like that of a Hajj and Umrah.   He said:   The Messenger of Allah said: 'Complete, complete, complete.' 

Sunan Tirmizi 586
The Book on Traveling

Ù„Ø°Øª Ø§Ù„Ø¯Ù†ÙŠØ§ Ø´ÙŠØ¨Øª Ø¨Ø§Ù„Ù†ØºØµ
*Worldly pleasures are mingled with distress/misery.*

Whoever reflects upon the world will realize that it contains no pure pleasure at all. And if any pleasure is found, it is mixed with troubles that far outweigh the pleasure many times over.

He goes on to say....*Among such pleasures* _(which bring misery/distress)_ *are women*: perhaps the one thought beautiful does not remain so, or perhaps she does not love her husband. Once that is known (that she does not love her) he should keep away from her. Perhaps she betrays and that is destruction. And even if all desires are fulfilled (with the woman), the thought of separation (from her) adds more pain than the pleasure itself.

Page no. 489, Publication by Dar ul Qalam - Damishq (see on https://shamela.ws/book/12028/803)

Imam Ibn al-Jawzi (rahimahullah) said:

"My brothers, travel is decreed for us. So why do we seek to reside in an abode that is not ours to dwell in permanently? The years are stations, the months are stops, the days are miles, the breaths are steps, sins are obstacles, profit is Paradise, and loss is Hellfire."

[Bahru ad-Dumu, Chapter 9]

Authenticity please, may Allaah be pleased with all of us'

Memorizing the Qur'an After the Age of Fifty (50)

Shaykh 'Abd al-Mushin al-'Abbad - may Allah preserve and protect him - was asked in his home: Is an individual able to memorize the Qur'an after reaching the age of fifty?

He replied: Yes, and I am from those who memorized the Qur'an after the age of fifty! There were Companions (may Allah be pleased with them) who Islam reached them when they were older; despite that they memorized.

16th of Jumada al-Akhirah 1441H

He said: â€œA young boy from the people of Sham came to Medina at an age like yours. He was diligent and sought knowledge with us until death came to him. I saw at his funeral something I had never seen for anyone from our town, neither student nor scholar.â€
I saw all the scholars crowding around his bier. When the ruler saw this, he refrained from leading the prayer over him and said: â€œBring forward whoever you wish from among you.â€ So the scholars brought forward Rabiâ€™ah, then carried him to his grave.

And he said: â€œKnowledge has reached him.â€ The man asked him: â€œAnd what has reached you?â€
He said: â€œAllah gave me a rank in Paradise for every branch of knowledge I learned, but the ranks did not reach the level of the scholars. 02/09/2025, 6:49â€¯pm - Muzammil New: *Advices from al-ShÄfi'Ä« when your friend does a mistake*
______________________________

YÅ«nus ibn Ê¿Abd al-AÊ¿lÄ said that l-ShÄfiÊ¿Ä« said to me one day:
*O YÅ«nus, if you are informed of something you dislike about your friend, then beware of rushing to animosity and cutting the friendship bond, lest you become one of those who removed his certainty with a doubt. Rather, meet him and say to him: 'It has reached me about you such-and-such' and it is better that you name who informed you. If he denies it, then say to him: 'You are more truthful and more upright,' and do not add anything to that. And if he confesses to it and you see an excuse for it, then accept it from him. And if you do not see that, then say to him: 'What did you intend by what has reached me about you?' If he then mentions a matter as an excuse, accept it. And if he does not mention an excuse for it, and the path becomes constricted for you, then at that point establish it against him as a misdeed. Then, you have the choice: if you wish, you may repay him in equal without any addition, and if you wish, you may forgive him. And forgiveness is more conducive to TaqwÃ¡ and more profound in nobility due to the saying of AllÄh the Exalted: {And the recompense for an evil is an evil like thereof, but whoever pardons and makes reconciliation - his reward is from AllÄh} [al-ShÅ«rÄ: 40]. So, if your soul contests with you, urging for retaliation, then remember the good he did for you and do not diminish the remainder of his previous goodness because of this single misdeed for that is injustice in its very essence. And a righteous man used to say: 'May AllÄh have mercy on one who repaid me for my wrongdoing without adding to it, nor diminishing a right that was due to me.' O YÅ«nus, if you have a friend, hold fast to him with both your hands, for indeed, making a friend is difficult and parting from him is easy. And a righteous man used to compare the ease of parting from a friend to a young boy who throws a great stone into a well; its throwing is easy for him, but its removal is difficult even for strong, sturdy men. So this is my counsel to you. And SalÄm.*

04/09/2025, 5:44â€¯pm - +91 88229 56870: Imam ash-Shafi'ee - Poetry on how to respond to Fool:

"The fools speak to me with all vulgarity

So I hate to respond likewise in turn. they increase in their evil, so I increase in my patience"

Like an incense that becomes more fragrant when burned. So when the fool speaks do not respond, the strongest rebuttal is lack of acknowledgment.

If you address him he finds comfort, but if you ignore him he remains paralyzed

In another narration Imam ash-Shafi'i said: "If a fool speaks, do not answer him. The best answer to him is silence. If you answer him, it will only loosen his tongue. If you leave him, he will die of sadness."

Also ash-Shafi'i said: "A humiliation of knowledge is to argue with everyone who tries to argue with you, and to speak with everyone who tries to speak with you." "Manaqib ash-Shafi'i", 2/151,
